		<div class="mv-create-description">
			





<p>My spiced apple and pear loaf is the perfect cosy bake for cooler days. It&rsquo;s warmly spiced with cinnamon and nutmeg, filled with tender chunks of fresh apple and pear, and comes out soft, moist, and full of flavour. Whether enjoyed as an afternoon snack with a cuppa or slightly warmed with a dollop of cream, it&rsquo;s one of those comforting bakes that never disappoints. And yes, it&rsquo;ll make your kitchen smell like pure autumnal heaven.</p>

	<div class="mv-create-ingredients">
		<h3 class="mv-create-ingredients-title mv-create-title-secondary">Ingredients</h3>

											<ul>
									<li>
						3 cups plain flour					</li>
									<li>
						1 tbsp baking powder					</li>
									<li>
						1 cup caster sugar					</li>
									<li>
						1 tsp salt					</li>
									<li>
						1 tsp cinnamon					</li>
									<li>
						1/2 tsp ginger					</li>
									<li>
						pinch nutmeg					</li>
									<li>
						zest of 1 lemon					</li>
									<li>
						juice of half a lemon					</li>
									<li>
						3/4 cup vegetable oil					</li>
									<li>
						3 eggs					</li>
									<li>
						1 cup grated pear					</li>
									<li>
						1 cup grated apple					</li>
							</ul>
			</div>
		<div class="mv-create-hands-free"></div>
		<div class="mv-create-instructions mv-create-instructions-slot-v2">
		<h3 class="mv-create-instructions-title mv-create-title-secondary">Instructions</h3>
		<ol><li id="mv_create_44_1">Preheat oven to 160C. Grease and line 1 x 3lb loaf tin.</li><li id="mv_create_44_2">In a large mixing bowl, mix together dry ingredients.</li><li id="mv_create_44_3">Next, stir through wet ingredients and fruit, and mix<br>through until well combined.</li><li id="mv_create_44_4">Transfer batter to the prepared loaf tin and bake for 1 hr and 5<br>minutes, or until an inserted skewer comes out clean.</li><li id="mv_create_44_5">Remove loaf from the loaf tin and rest on a cooling rack for ten<br>minutes, prior to serving.<br></li></ol>	</div>

		<div class="mv-create-notes-content">
			<p></p><p>This is a very thick mixture, similar to muffins but don't worry - the moisture from the apple and pear makes it work!</p>

<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Spiced Apple and Pear Loaf</h2>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img data-recalc-dims="1" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1254" height="1254" <h3 class="wp-block-heading">Office Fruit and Cake Nostalgia</h3>



<p>Every Monday, our office gets a massive basket of fruit. It sounds lovely in theory, but by Friday it&rsquo;s a graveyard of apples and pears that nobody wants &ndash; which is exactly why I love it! Because those end-of-week leftovers are perfect for baking, and that&rsquo;s how this spiced apple and pear loaf came about &ndash; it&rsquo;s soft, comforting, and full of flavour. A warm slice of this loaf with a cup of tea on a grey Scottish afternoon? Yes please.</p>



<p>Apple teacakes were a staple when I was growing up. If we were visiting anyone, there&rsquo;d always be a homemade cake coming with us &ndash; usually fruity, always spiced. It was just the done thing back in the 90&rsquo;s in Western Sydney. My family were serial hosts and serial visitors, so someone was always baking (or buying a cheeky loaf from the local Viet bakery). This loaf reminds me of those days &ndash; it&rsquo;s familiar and humble and just sweet enough to feel like a treat without being over the top.</p>



<p>Since moving to Scotland, I&rsquo;ve had to explain more than once that my version of a teacake isn&rsquo;t a marshmallowy biscuit covered in chocolate. An Aussie teacake is simple and spiced and served thickly sliced with salted butter. It&rsquo;s not fancy, it&rsquo;s not trendy &ndash; it&rsquo;s just <em>good</em>. And this spiced apple and pear loaf? It&rsquo;s exactly that.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-large"><img data-recalc-dims="1" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1254" height="1254" src="https://i0.wp.com/cookingwithbry.com/wp-content/uploads/Spiced-Apple-and-Pear-Loaf-Recipe-12.jpg?resize=1254%2C1254&#038;ssl=1" alt="spiced apple and pear loaf" class="wp-image-13227" <h3 class="wp-block-heading">Easy Enough to Wing It</h3>



<p>What I love about this loaf is how low-stress it is. Baking usually wants you to be all scientific with scales and timers, but this one is beautifully forgiving. A little extra spice, a bit more fruit, a splash more lemon &ndash; she copes. You can tweak it depending on what&rsquo;s hanging around &ndash; I&rsquo;ve tossed in leftover dried cranberries before. Once I even added orange zest instead of lemon because that&rsquo;s all I had (well, the fruit basket had&hellip;)</p>



<p>You don&rsquo;t need anything special to make it either &ndash; just a bowl, a spoon, and a bit of enthusiasm. It comes together quickly and it smells so good when it&rsquo;s baking that I tend to hover around the kitchen pretending I&rsquo;m doing something else. Bonus points that it slices well and keeps moist for a few days. Not that it ever lasts that long in my house!</p>



<p>This is the sort of recipe I turn to when I want the comfort of baking without the faff. I can throw it together while half-distracted, clean the kitchen before it&rsquo;s done, and have something warm and spiced to show for it. It&rsquo;s also brilliant if you&rsquo;re trying to save sad fruit from going to waste. Soft pears? Slightly wrinkled apples? In they go.</p>

<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Every Bite Is Different</h3>



<p>The thing about this spiced apple and pear loaf is that no one can agree on what makes it so good. Some people swear it&rsquo;s the ginger. Others are adamant the lemon zest makes it. One person told me it reminded them of their gran&rsquo;s pudding, which was a lovely moment. I like that everyone seems to taste something different in it. It makes for fun conversations over tea.</p>



<p>Food like this has a way of getting people talking. I&rsquo;ve had mates pause mid-mouthful and ask what&rsquo;s in it, trying to guess the spices or work out what gives it that particular zing. And I love that!! I love how a simple bake can invite connection and a bit of joy. It&rsquo;s also kind of magic how the flavours mellow and develop after a day or two, which makes it excellent for sharing (if you&rsquo;re that way inclined).</p>



<p>Some bakes are meant to be showy, but this one isn&rsquo;t. I don&rsquo;t bake for show, I bake for love. And this cake is&nbsp; the kind of thing you make to fill your kitchen with warmth, to use up a glut of fruit, or just because it&rsquo;s Thursday and you need something nice. It&rsquo;s a gentle loaf. Friendly, familiar, not trying too hard &ndash; just the way I like it.</p>

<h3 class="wp-block-heading">Ingredients Breakdown</h3>



<p>This spiced apple and pear loaf starts with plain flour and baking powder &ndash; nothing fancy. A bit of caster sugar adds sweetness, and salt sharpens it all up just enough. The real fun is in the spices. I go for a warm mix of cinnamon, ginger, and nutmeg &ndash; not too much, but enough to make the whole house smell like something cosy is happening.</p>



<p>Lemon zest and a squeeze of juice add brightness and lift the flavour, keeping the loaf from being too heavy. I use vegetable oil instead of butter &ndash; it gives the crumb a soft, almost sponge-like texture. Eggs bind everything together, and the fruit does the rest. Grated pear and apple melt into the mix, keeping it moist and naturally sweet.</p>



<p>It&rsquo;s a lovely combination. Nothing outrageous. Just good ingredients doing what they&rsquo;re supposed to. It&rsquo;s the kind of loaf that&rsquo;s best enjoyed in thick slices with a bit of butter and a cup of tea. Preferably while hiding from the rain and pretending the washing up will do itself.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image size-full"><img data-recalc-dims="1" loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1080" height="1920" src="https://i0.wp.com/cookingwithbry.com/wp-content/uploads/Spiced-Apple-Pear-Loaf-Recipe-Pin.jpg?resize=1080%2C1920&#038;ssl=1" alt="spiced apple and pear loaf" class="wp-image-21748" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/cookingwithbry.com/wp-content/uploads/Spiced-Apple-Pear-Loaf-Recipe-Pin.jpg?w=1080&amp;ssl=1 1080w, https://i0.wp.com/cookingwithbry.com/wp-content/uploads/Spiced-Apple-Pear-Loaf-Recipe-Pin.jpg?resize=169%2C300&amp;ssl=1 169w, https://i0.wp.com/cookingwithbry.com/wp-content/uploads/Spiced-Apple-Pear-Loaf-Recipe-Pin.jpg?resize=768%2C1365&amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/cookingwithbry.com/wp-content/uploads/Spiced-Apple-Pear-Loaf-Recipe-Pin.jpg?resize=864%2C1536&amp;ssl=1 864w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1080px) 100vw, 1080px"></figure>

							<a href="https://cookingwithbry.com/slow-cooked-goat-goulash-recipe/"><img data-mobile-version="" src="https://i0.wp.com/cookingwithbry.com/wp-content/uploads/Slow-Cooked-Goat-Goulash.webp?fit=1080%2C1080&ssl=1&resize=480%2C307.69230769231" alt="This Slow-Cooked Goat Goulash is hearty comfort in a pot. Tender goat simmers away with sweet and smoked paprika, tomatoes, and peppers until the meat practically falls apart. It’s rich, warming, and full of depth – the kind of dish that fills the kitchen with mouthwatering aromas as it bubbles in the oven. I love serving it with crusty bread, mash, or buttered noodles. A rustic, flavour-packed recipe that proves goat deserves a spot at the table." loading="lazy" /></a>

			<h4 class="font-family-3 about-author-name"><a href="https://cookingwithbry.com/author/admin_bry/" title="Posts by Bry" rel="author">Bry</a></h4>

			<div class="about-author-bio">
				Bry is a Brisbane-based food writer and the voice behind Cooking with Bry. Raised in Sydney and shaped by years of living and eating her way across the world, she brings a well-travelled palate to everyday cooking. Bry believes comfort food is the heart of a happy kitchen, and her recipes reflect that: simple, satisfying dishes made for real people with real lives. No fuss, just flavour.			</div><!-- .about-author-bio -->
